  //<![CDATA[
    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }
    
    function initAppleId() {
      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app', 
        scope : 'name email',
        redirectURI: 'https://www.goodreads.com/apple_users/sign_in_with_apple_web',
        state: 'apple_oauth_state_2a115612-236d-4c4c-8832-80a752e2f6df'
      });
    }
    
    var initializeSiwa = function() {
      var APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL =  "https://appleid.cdn-apple.com/appleauth/static/jsapi/appleid/1/en_US/appleid.auth.js"
      loadScript(APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL, initAppleId);
    };

<span id="freeTextContainer234707268754027337">Surprises abound and sparks ignite in the highly anticipated, utterly romantic companion to <i>My Life Next Door</i><br/><br/>Tim Mason was The Boy Most Likely To:<br/>- find the liquor cabinet blindfolded<br/>- need a liver transplant<br/>- drive his car into a house<br/><br/>Alice Garrett was The Girl Most Likely To:<br/>- well, not date her little brother’s baggage-burdened best friend, for starters.<br/><br/>For Tim, it woul</span>
  <span id="freeText234707268754027337" style="display:none">Surprises abound and sparks ignite in the highly anticipated, utterly romantic companion to <i>My Life Next Door</i><br /><br />Tim Mason was The Boy Most Likely To:<br />- find the liquor cabinet blindfolded<br />- need a liver transplant<br />- drive his car into a house<br /><br />Alice Garrett was The Girl Most Likely To:<br />- well, not date her little brother’s baggage-burdened best friend, for starters.<br /><br />For Tim, it wouldn’t be smart to fall for Alice. For Alice, nothing could be scarier than falling for Tim. But Tim has never been known for making the smart choice, and Alice is starting to wonder if the “smart” choice is always the right one. When these two crash into each other, they crash hard. <br /><br />Then the unexpected consequences of Tim’s wild days come back to shock him. He finds himself in a situation that isn’t all it appears to be, that he never could have predicted . . . but maybe should have.<br /><br />And Alice is caught in the middle. <br /><br />Told in Tim’s and Alice’s distinctive, disarming, entirely compelling voices, this return to the world of <i>My Life Next Door</i> is a story about failing first, trying again, and having to decide whether to risk it all once more.</span>

<div id="review_705976310" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/705976310" />
    <a title="Danielle (Love at First Page)" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1312450-danielle-love-at-first-page"><img alt="Danielle (Love at First Page)" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1578285312p2/1312450.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/705976310?book_show_action=true">Aug 28, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Danielle (Love at First Page)" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Danielle (Love at First Page)" href="/user/show/1312450-danielle-love-at-first-page">Danielle (Love at First Page)</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9780803741423" href="/book/show/24611582-the-boy-most-likely-to">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1312450-danielle-love-at-first-page?shelf=contemporary">contemporary</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1312450-danielle-love-at-first-page?shelf=cover-love">cover-love</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1312450-danielle-love-at-first-page?shelf=e-arc">e-arc</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1312450-danielle-love-at-first-page?shelf=daddys-girl">daddys-girl</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1312450-danielle-love-at-first-page?shelf=own-physical-book">own-physical-book</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1312450-danielle-love-at-first-page?shelf=genre-young-adult">genre-young-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1312450-danielle-love-at-first-page?shelf=read-in-2015">read-in-2015</a>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer705976310" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6212359580320346984"><b>3.5-4 stars</b><br/><br/>Where do I even start with this review? I have been waiting for Tim Mason’s book for years now, having first met and fell in love with him in <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/12294652.My_Life_Next_Door' title='My Life Next Door by Huntley Fitzpatrick' rel='nofollow noopener'>My Life Next Door</a>. Reckless, charming, charismatic, down on his luck, red-headed Tim Mason. His was a happy ending I wanted more than anything. I definitely built up in my head how I imagined this would go, which is probably where things went wrong. While my rating is a positive one, when I think about <i>The Boy Most Likely To</i> there’s a hole there</span>
  <span id="freeText6212359580320346984" style="display:none"><b>3.5-4 stars</b><br /><br />Where do I even start with this review? I have been waiting for Tim Mason’s book for years now, having first met and fell in love with him in <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/12294652.My_Life_Next_Door" title="My Life Next Door by Huntley Fitzpatrick" rel="nofollow noopener">My Life Next Door</a>. Reckless, charming, charismatic, down on his luck, red-headed Tim Mason. His was a happy ending I wanted more than anything. I definitely built up in my head how I imagined this would go, which is probably where things went wrong. While my rating is a positive one, when I think about <i>The Boy Most Likely To</i> there’s a hole there waiting be filled with my expectations. <br /><br /><b>What I wanted:</b> A summertime romance, light and lovely and swoony with just the right amount of heartbreak. <br /><br /><b>What I got:</b> A story full of complications and heartache, subplots I wasn’t expecting, a romance that was barely felt until more than halfway through the book. <br /><br />This isn’t necessarily a bad thing, but while reading I just kept thinking this is not the romance story I envisioned for Tim, which caused some frustration. Like we got of Sam and Jase in <i>My Life Next Door</i>, I wanted more of a focus on Tim and Alice’s relationship. I wanted the swoons to be out in full force. Did I still love Tim and Alice together? Absolutely. He’s a bit of mess – an AA member, kicked out of school and his parents’ house – but he’s trying to pick up the pieces and start over. Tim may not have his life figured out, but he’s a genuine guy, warm and funny and someone you want to be around. Alice is his opposite, a control freak with a heavy load of responsibly on her shoulders. At first she sees Tim as just another person in her life she has to take care of, but there’s attraction there and eventually their relationship takes a much different shape. It moves slowly, and I would have liked many more scenes of them together, but what we do get is toe-curling. Huntley Fitzpatrick knows her way around delicious kisses, and once again she gives us a memorable “first time” that is so beautifully written. Tim and Alice have a few ups and downs throughout the story as they deal with their own personal issues, but I did like their growing friendship and chemistry. <br /><br />Like I said though, the book has its hand in many different cookie jars. As we’ve come to expect from Huntely’s books, the theme of family is very much present. It was great being back with the Garretts and seeing this big family with an even bigger heart stick together through everything. The kids are also pretty stinkin’ adorable. But even they get waylaid by other characters and subplots I didn’t care for, like Alice’s ex-boyfriend and what I’ll refer to as Tim’s situation. I have to be vague to avoid spoilers, but I wasn’t all that crazy about the catalyst for Tim’s growth. I loved his incredibly sincere and sympathetic voice and I loved seeing such an easy-to-love guy become a better person, but that story line didn’t always ring true for me. It was also hard to enjoy it when I wanted the focus to be on other ones.<br /><br />Maybe it wasn't quite fair of me to have expected <i>My Life Next Door</i> 2.0, but that’s the story I wanted and letting go of that wasn’t easy. Like all of Huntely’s couples, I believe in Tim and Alice’s love story wholeheartedly, I just wanted more of it. I think this is a book that definitely deserves a re-read; maybe now that I know what to expect I could better appreciate the story for what it is. All-in-all <i>The Boy Most Likely To</i> is still one of the better young adult contemporaries out there. I’ll be glad to have Tim’s cover right next to Jase’s on my bookshelf. <br /><br /><i>Thanks to Netgalley and the publisher for sending me e-ARC in exchange for my honest review.</i><br /><br />This review can also be found at <a href="http://www.loveatfirstpage.org/2015/08/17/arc-review-the-boy-most-likely-to/" rel="nofollow noopener">Love at First Page</a>.</span>

          </span>

<div id="review_1423904022" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1423904022" />
    <a title="C.G. Drews" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/11375137-c-g-drews"><img alt="C.G. Drews" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1521552918p2/11375137.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1423904022?book_show_action=true">Oct 23, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="C.G. Drews" class="user" itemprop="url" name="C.G. Drews" href="/user/show/11375137-c-g-drews">C.G. Drews</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9781405280396" href="/book/show/28756053-the-boy-most-likely-to">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/11375137-c-g-drews?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/11375137-c-g-drews?shelf=contemporary">contemporary</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/11375137-c-g-drews?shelf=read-2016">read-2016</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1423904022" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer10390586493562883777">Ohhhh <b>that was adorably tragic and I LOVED IT SO MUCH MY HEART HURTS.</b> I was such a fan of Tim when he was a secondary character in <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/12294652.My_Life_Next_Door' title='My Life Next Door by Huntley Fitzpatrick' rel='nofollow noopener'>My Life Next Door</a>. And honestly??? This book is like 1000% better with it being focused on precious tragic loser Tim and angry snappy heroic Alice. I <i>love</i> them. I will squish them with enthusiasm. Or mabye not, because that would be rude probably.<br/><br/>** NOTE: I will talk about <i>one</i> spoiler in this book without spoiler tags! It is a plot twist and happens around the 100-pa</span>
  <span id="freeText10390586493562883777" style="display:none">Ohhhh <b>that was adorably tragic and I LOVED IT SO MUCH MY HEART HURTS.</b> I was such a fan of Tim when he was a secondary character in <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/12294652.My_Life_Next_Door" title="My Life Next Door by Huntley Fitzpatrick" rel="nofollow noopener">My Life Next Door</a>. And honestly??? This book is like 1000% better with it being focused on precious tragic loser Tim and angry snappy heroic Alice. I <i>love</i> them. I will squish them with enthusiasm. Or mabye not, because that would be rude probably.<br /><br />** NOTE: I will talk about <i>one</i> spoiler in this book without spoiler tags! It is a plot twist and happens around the 100-page mark. But it colours the book SO MUCH I just think it's impossible to discuss the book without talking about it, yes?? But if you want to go in blind <u>don't read on obviously</u>.<br /><br />ANYWAY! MOVING FORWARD! HUZZH!<br /><br /><b>My favourite part, of course, is Tim and getting to be in his perspective.</b> He's sassy and actually quite smart and he covers everything that hurts him with sarcastic/sassy remarks. IT'S tRAGIC OKAY?! His humour is his armour. Basically everyone has labelled him the alcoholic, loser, drop-out, jerk...the "boy most likely to fail at life" basically. It's super sad. He's <i>trying</i> to get his life back no track but like no one believes in him. THAT MUST BE SUPER HARD. OMG MY PRECIOUS BUNDLE OF TRYING.<br /><br />Also I really like how this book talks about <b>addictions and recovery.</b> Tim is a recovering alcoholic. I see a TON of YA books about teens who are falling down the drugs/alcoholic route....and that's usually what happens. THEY FALL. I want to see more books where they're picking back up again. <b>So I think this book is very much needed</b> especially when it tells the other side of the story when it come sto addiction.<br /><br /><b>Then there's Alice...AHHH ALICE.</b> She's so angry! And wonderful! And she totally takes zero crap from anyone. She does a lot of looking-after-her-gazillion-siblings because of Mrs. Garrett being pregnant and Mr. Garrett still being in rehab after the accident in My Life Next Door.<br /><br /><b>AND CAN WE JUST TALK ABOUT HOW AWESOME THE GARRETT FAMILY IS?!??!?</b> I looove them so much. Big family <i>win</i>. And since Tim lives above their garage, we like get sooo much more Garretts. It's glorious.<br /><br />I request a spin off for each Garrett child immediately. (Although I maintain George doesn't act like a 4yo...he's far too eloquent and well spoken. Either that or he's Autistic and it doesn't write him as an ASD kid so, idek. But the rest of the siblings/family dynamics are perfect.)<br /><br /><b>Okay, and then there's the fact that: Tim is also a father.</b> This part of the story line ABSOLUTELY GOT ME. I love small human mortals. They are adorable. I babysit my sister's collection frequently. But like imagine being 17 and suddenly "hey you're a dad". OMG IT WAS SUCH A PLOT TWIST. Most of the book is Tim looking after his little Calvin while the mother tries to get the adoption thing going.<br /><br />(BTW, the mother is horrible. Like she totally drives up, says "Hey Tim you have a son, can you babysit for a few nights?" and dumps the child and leaves. She has NO attachment to her baby, it's actually disturbing????)<br /><br />TIM'S ATTEMPTS AT BEING A FATHER ARE ADORABLE AND GORGEOUS AND BROKE MY FEELS BASICALLY. <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[I will forever be devastated Cal wasn't even his. 3 I wanted Tim to raise him and just toss stereotypes and end up being an awesome teen dad and just ajfdksalfd I wanted it so bad. *sobs* But no Cal got adopted out. <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br /><br /><b>The actual writing, I did find a little clunky at times.</b> My <i>biggest</i> pet peeve was the fact that it's <b>dual narrated, but both in 1st person...with NO INDICATION ON WHOSE CHAPTER IT IS.</b> Just arghar agh ghgarghghg, okay?!? It drove me crazy. I had such a hard time figuring out if it was Tim or Alice speaking sometimes. And I do think the writing clunked often. It got better as it went on. <b>And it was way too long.</b> 500-pages is ALWAYS too long for a contemporary, in my opinion. Less blather! More action! Huzh!<br /><br /><b>ALL IN ALL: this book absolutely wrapped around my soul and gave me all the feels.</b> It was equal parts noble and tragic and feelsy and adorable. I loved how Tim and Alice made tons of mistakes but kept giving each other a bit of room to fail. I LOVE Tim's character development. Calvin is adorable. &lt;33 There was actual ice cream. SO much sass. And a dead owl in the freezer at one point. The chaos of a big family. Ohhhhhhhh....<b>I just like.</b></span>
  <a data-text-id="10390586493562883777" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

<span id="freeTextContainer10497606684360917559">I waited for this book for what felt like forever, but then when it finally released, I waited another 2 years before reading it. I just knew I would love Tim in this book just based on what we got of him from <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/12294652.My_Life_Next_Door' title='My Life Next Door by Huntley Fitzpatrick' rel='nofollow noopener'>My Life Next Door</a>.   <span id="freeText10497606684360917559" style="display:none">I waited for this book for what felt like forever, but then when it finally released, I waited another 2 years before reading it. I just knew I would love Tim in this book just based on what we got of him from <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/12294652.My_Life_Next_Door" title="My Life Next Door by Huntley Fitzpatrick" rel="nofollow noopener">My Life Next Door</a>. The love story, I felt wasn't as epic as Jase and Sam's but it was still great. I think the issue was that I just couldn't really relate to Alice much. Her POV just lacked something. When I was reading her POV, it didn't really generate much emotion out of me. I almost wish the book was written entirely in Tim's POV. I really loved his character growth and just how he handled the situations he was faced with. I also really love the Garrett family. I wish there was another book just so I could get more of them. <br><br><br>******* Initial Reaction: Oct 22, 2013 *******<br><br>I think I just died and went to book heaven<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380914559ra/3216681.gif" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>So excited to find out that this is Tim's story and that Jase and Samantha will appear in it...but gosh, 2015 release date!?!?!<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1382724231ra/6147938.gif" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><br>I mean...<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380222758ra/675205.gif" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1382724716ra/6148393.gif" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>June 2015 seems like forever and a day away!</span>

<div id="review_1283752388" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1283752388" />
    <a title="Jaime Arkin" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5293701-jaime-arkin"><img alt="Jaime Arkin" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1303353688p2/5293701.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1283752388?book_show_action=true">May 18, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Jaime Arkin" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Jaime Arkin" href="/user/show/5293701-jaime-arkin">Jaime Arkin</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5293701-jaime-arkin?shelf=2015">2015</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5293701-jaime-arkin?shelf=can-t-frickin-wait">can-t-frickin-wait</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5293701-jaime-arkin?shelf=ya">ya</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5293701-jaime-arkin?shelf=omg-i-have-to-have-it">omg-i-have-to-have-it</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5293701-jaime-arkin?shelf=series">series</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5293701-jaime-arkin?shelf=read-in-2015">read-in-2015</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5293701-jaime-arkin?shelf=penguin">penguin</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1283752388" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer4293034222048101113">I’ve been waiting almost three years for this book. Since the day I turned the last page in My Life Next Door I had to know more about Tim! I even mentioned it in my <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/265310685?book_show_action=false' rel='nofollow noopener'>review!</a> He was such a big part of MLND and his character was so charismatic I knew that there had to be more to his story. I can’t even tell you how excited I was when I found out that this was something that was going to happen in real life. <br/><br/>I’m not even sure how to review this book because there is so much that happens that I <b>can’</b></span>
  <span id="freeText4293034222048101113" style="display:none">I’ve been waiting almost three years for this book. Since the day I turned the last page in My Life Next Door I had to know more about Tim! I even mentioned it in my <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/265310685?book_show_action=false" rel="nofollow noopener">review!</a> He was such a big part of MLND and his character was so charismatic I knew that there had to be more to his story. I can’t even tell you how excited I was when I found out that this was something that was going to happen in real life. <br /><br />I’m not even sure how to review this book because there is so much that happens that I <b>can’t</b> tell you about without spoiling the journey. So let me first say this. Huntley Fitzpatrick does complicated families like no other. She creates incredibly layered characters that could be anyone in your family. She creates a beautiful story filled with bits of heartbreak, stolen moments, romance and unimaginable amounts of struggle but always, always filled with heart. <br /><br />This is of course Tim’s story… but it’s also Alice’s story. Alice is Jase’s older sister. She’s got her whole life ahead of her yet, she takes on the problems of her parents and family as wholly her own. She has this intense desire to solve all the issues and be the solution to the problems that arise, only life is never that easy, because it involves giving up things she’s been planning for and even then there is no guarantee that the problems will go away. <br /><br />Tim… you guys remember Tim. He uses humor as a defense and his self-deprecation is more than just making fun of himself. He’s hid behind drugs and alcohol for longer than one can imagine at the age of 17 and he’s come to realize with the help of his friends that there is more to life than getting so wasted you can’t remember things. But with that realization comes the responsibilities that he’d been avoiding for all those years and the things he’s screwed up along the way. I can’t tell you how many times I wish he were real so I could pull him close and squeeze him tight, even if he wouldn’t let me because you honestly have to love his outlook on life. <br /><br /><b>
  <i>She moves closer; smells like I’ve always thought Hawaii would, green and sweet, earthy, sun and sea mixed together, smoky warm. Her greenish gray eyes, flecks of gold too – <br /><br />“You’ve only got one dimple,” she says.<br /><br />“That a drawback? I had two, but I misplaced one on a particularly hard night.”<br /><br />She gives my shoulder a shove. “You joke about everything.”<br /><br />“Everything is pretty funny,” I say, trying to sit up but sinking back, my back groaning. “If you look at it the right way.”<br /><br />“How do you know you’re looking at it the right way?”<br /><br />Alice’s head’s lowered, she’s still circling an index finger in the sand, only inches from brushing her knuckles past my stomach. The morning air is still and calm – no sound of the waves, even.<br /><br />“If it's funny,” I wheeze, “you’re looking at it the right way.”</i>
</b><br /><br />Tim is a born flirt and Alice, well she doesn’t really put up with his shit … which oddly enough makes them perfect for each other and seeing the evolution of their relationship, the sweet moments, the passionate moments and the trials and tribulations… because there are plenty of those was just everything I could have hoped for and more. <br /> <br />Ultimately this story is about family and knowing that it’s not always the family that we’re born into that has our back and will be there to support us through our mistakes, nor will it be the people we share DNA with that we come to lean on and find a home with. <br /><br />I know that this seems somewhat vague, that’s intentional because there are some things that I can’t divulge. You’ll have to read to find out what those things are, and I promise you'll thank me for letting you experience it as Tim's story unfolds. <br /><br />All that said, if there was one thing that I didn't really care for, it would be Brad’s story. Or his involvement… I don’t know how to say this without giving anything away, but I’ll just say that I feel like his part in this story felt unfinished and and not explored enough to ultimately have him be a part of this story. <br /><br />BUT that is minor and not a huge part of what's going on and I honestly only noticed it when I turned the last page and realized where that left off. <br /><br />Oh!! Also - glimpses of Jase *swoon* and Sam and the rest of the Garrets only make this story even more amazing! If you thought you loved George in My Life Next Door, be prepared for even more cute from him and the rest of the gang. <br /><br />Grab this if you’re looking for an incredible story of life and love and finding family where you least expect it. Once again Fitzpatrick made me fall in love with her characters and the Garrett family in ways I never could have anticipated! <br /><br />Thank you Huntley for the advanced copy in exchange for my honest thoughts! <br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="4293034222048101113" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1369280253" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1369280253" />
    <a title="Ferdy" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4596358-ferdy"><img alt="Ferdy" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1487898103p2/4596358.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1369280253?book_show_action=true">Aug 20, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Ferdy" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Ferdy" href="/user/show/4596358-ferdy">Ferdy</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition " href="/book/show/24883170-the-boy-most-likely-to">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4596358-ferdy?shelf=blah-romance">blah-romance</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4596358-ferdy?shelf=blah">blah</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4596358-ferdy?shelf=annoying-kids">annoying-kids</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4596358-ferdy?shelf=awful-main-character">awful-main-character</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4596358-ferdy?shelf=contemporary">contemporary</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
                  <em>
                    This review has been hidden because it contains spoilers. To view it,
                    <a href="#" onclick="Effect.toggle(&#39;reviewTextContainer1369280253&#39;); return false;">click here.</a>
                  </em>
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1369280253" class="readable"
                    style="display:none"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7365972244126266328"><b>Spoilers</b><br/><br/>Really disappointing. Predictable story, flat romance, and bland/insufferable main characters. <br/><br/>-Didn't feel any connection between Alice/Tim, their romance was so hollow and rushed.<br/>Tim didn't give a damn about Alice, he was only ever concerned about his own problems/feelings and then at the end he was all about Cal (which was super boring). The only reason Tim seemed to even want Alice was because he found her hot and liked her family, I never got the sense he truly knew her or even care</span>
  <span id="freeText7365972244126266328" style="display:none"><b>Spoilers</b><br /><br />Really disappointing. Predictable story, flat romance, and bland/insufferable main characters. <br /><br />-Didn't feel any connection between Alice/Tim, their romance was so hollow and rushed.<br />Tim didn't give a damn about Alice, he was only ever concerned about his own problems/feelings and then at the end he was all about Cal (which was super boring). The only reason Tim seemed to even want Alice was because he found her hot and liked her family, I never got the sense he truly knew her or even cared for her, his feelings for her were so cold (well, except for when he was horny). <br />Alice on the other hand was desperate for sulky-attention-seeking-loser Tim despite having a million other problems to deal with. Their relationship wasn't interesting or believable, they had no passion or chemistry. Them exchanging I-love-you's after dating for all of five minutes was laughable, it came out of nowhere.<br /><br />-I preferred Alice and Tim's relationship with their families than each other, it was far more interesting reading about their interactions with their parents/siblings than the flat romance they had going on. <br /><br />-Didn't buy Alice wanting to be with Tim after the Cal reveal, she was already sick of being a second mother of sorts to her siblings, so her accepting Tim/Cal as a package didn't seem likely. Why would she want to be saddled with a teen boyfriend with alcohol problems and a newborn baby when she had so much going on in her own life?! I can't believe she didn't walk away from Tim's car crash life, her staying didn't fit with her personality or circumstances. And then Alice getting upset at the end when she found out Cal wasn't Tim's was even more nonsensical, in reality she would be relieved not to be stuck being a teen stepmother when she'd spent so much time resenting and stressing about playing mummy to her siblings.<br /><br />-Really couldn't stand Tim, he caused all sorts of problems for himself and I didn't feel sorry for him one bit. He was a whiny, self-pitying brat. <br />I hated how lame and sleazy he was when it came to Alice, he was such an immature perv. Then there was him getting angry and bitchy whenever Alice or Hester deigned to say or do something he didn't like, he would snap at them and get all pissed over nothing. At times he sounded like a misogynistic prick, especially when it came to Hester's relationship with Cal, he was a total hypocrite. Also, him not getting a paternity test when he found about Calvin was beyond ridiculous, that should have been the first thing he did. <br /><br />-This was all there was to Tim:<br /><br />Oh no, I drink and do drugs and sleep around and flunk out of school and my parents are disappointed in me. Poor me, my life's so hard. No understands me, pity me. <br /><br />Oh no, Hester just told me I'm the father of her baby. I don't even remember sleeping with her because I was apparently in a drunken stupor, but that's not suspicious at all. Oh well, I won't do a DNA test to confirm its mine because it has red hair and that means it has to be mine because no-one else in the world has red hair.<br /><br />Oh no, Hester doesn't love baby Calvin like a mother should. It doesn't matter that she's a teenager and a first time mum or that I'm a crappy dad myself, I'm still going to judge her and act like she's awful. Poor me.<br /><br />Oh no, Alice said/did something totally reasonable but I'm going to take it as an insult and call her out on it and make her feel guilty, that way she can look like she's done something wrong and I'll come out smelling like roses. Ugh.<br /><br />-What the hell was Tim's problem with the name Calvin? He actually called it a 'pussy name' and then proceeded to call his son Cal instead. Ugh, he was an absolute idiot.<br /><br />-Hated all the parts where Tim narrated Cal's 'thoughts', I guess it was meant to be cute or something but it was just cringey.<br /><br />-I was so pissed at Tim inviting himself into the Garret house and eating all of their food when they barely had enough for themselves. He never stopped to think about their struggles, everything was about him. He was a selfish, entitled, greedy git.<br /><br />-Hated Alice's parents for leaving her to deal with the kids and finances, I know Alice's dad was hurt and the mum was pregnant but they shouldn't have expected Alice to pick up the pieces and put so much pressure on her. Absolutely detested them for having so many kids when they could barely afford the ones they had, not only that they couldn't even look after them properly without getting the older teens to do the bulk of the work. Alice and Jase should have been getting on with their own lives, not constantly looking after their bratty siblings.<br /><br />-I rolled my eyes at Alice saying she'd never climaxed before yet was able to the first time she and Tim got it on. Yea, I doubt Tim could be that good when he'd only ever had drunk sex before.<br /><br />-The dialogue was really at bad times, it was so stilted and forced.<br /><br />-I remember liking the Garretts and all the younger kids in the first book, but I found them annoying in this, especially George/Patsy and the parents. <br /><br />Nowhere near as good as <i>My life Next Door</i>, Tim was an awful character and the whole Calvin arc was boring. The only thing I really enjoyed were the few Nan and Sam/Jase scenes.<br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="7365972244126266328" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

<div id="review_762773778" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/762773778" />
    <a title="Arlene" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1746727-arlene"><img alt="Arlene" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1347048609p2/1746727.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/762773778?book_show_action=true">Nov 11, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Arlene" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Arlene" href="/user/show/1746727-arlene">Arlene</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9780803741423" href="/book/show/24611582-the-boy-most-likely-to">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1746727-arlene?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1746727-arlene?shelf=read-2015">read-2015</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1746727-arlene?shelf=ya-contemporary">ya-contemporary</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1746727-arlene?shelf=arc">arc</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer762773778" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8757993178079633241">I was really excited about diving into the second installment of Huntley Fitzpatrick’s novel <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/12294652.My_Life_Next_Door' title='My Life Next Door by Huntley Fitzpatrick' rel='nofollow noopener'>My Life Next Door</a>. I remember that book being a perfect summer read that satisfied my YA contemporary craving that never ceases to wane. Unfortunately, <b>The Boy Most Likely To</b> didn’t quite hit the mark for me in so many subtle ways.<br/><br/>Having met Tim Mason and Alice Garrett in the first book, I was looking forward to seeing them get their own installment. I remember Jase’s best friend Tim being a hot mess tha</span>
  <span id="freeText8757993178079633241" style="display:none">I was really excited about diving into the second installment of Huntley Fitzpatrick’s novel <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/12294652.My_Life_Next_Door" title="My Life Next Door by Huntley Fitzpatrick" rel="nofollow noopener">My Life Next Door</a>. I remember that book being a perfect summer read that satisfied my YA contemporary craving that never ceases to wane. Unfortunately, <b>The Boy Most Likely To</b> didn’t quite hit the mark for me in so many subtle ways.<br /><br />Having met Tim Mason and Alice Garrett in the first book, I was looking forward to seeing them get their own installment. I remember Jase’s best friend Tim being a hot mess that kept making mistake after mistake. Well, as the title indicates, he’s the boy most likely to not finish high school, get drunk night after night, and seriously disappoint his family because of his choices. <br /><br />Alice is Jase’s older sister that seems to be struggling in a different sort of way. She's the backbone of her family that is keeping them afloat as their father recovers from an accident that left him badly injured. As she balances finishing nursing school, taking care of her siblings, running the household and helping with the family business, she knows that last thing she has time for is to fall for Tim that seems to be stumbling through life.<br /><br />Together these two uncover an attraction and work toward finding a middle ground in the mess that is their life. <br /><br />Well first off, let me share that it took me three LONG weeks to finish this book. It wasn’t quite what I had hoped for, and I had such a hard time connecting with these characters. I also had a difficult time picking up on the cadence of the dual narrative. I never seemed to find my stride and enjoy Alice and Tim’s journey. I didn’t have a difficult time with the age difference, but it would have been nice for Tim to at least be of legal age… that would have been an easier pill to swallow for some of the stuff that happened in this book.<br /><br />If I had to pull anything positive from this book, I have to admit that I really liked the ending despite how long it took me to get there. <br /><br />Overall, not quite what I was expecting for a summer, contemporary read. It seemed to have missed the mark for me in more ways than one.</span>
  <a data-text-id="8757993178079633241" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_731677043" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/731677043" />
    <a title="Tsukushi (Maan)" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5323192-tsukushi-maan"><img alt="Tsukushi (Maan)" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1586515469p2/5323192.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">

<div id="review_1350009115" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1350009115" />
    <a title="Jen Ryland" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/6497049-jen-ryland"><img alt="Jen Ryland" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1499993823p2/6497049.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1350009115?book_show_action=true">Jul 30, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Jen Ryland" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Jen Ryland" href="/user/show/6497049-jen-ryland">Jen Ryland</a>
      </span>

          added it


          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9780803741423" href="/book/show/24611582-the-boy-most-likely-to">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1350009115" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16079556738715604385">So ... whoa! This book was not at all what I expected. I did like <b>Boy Most Likely To</b>, but it took me some time to shift my mental gears around and adjust to the loss of the story I thought I was getting and warm up to the one I got. I'll talk about the non-spoilery stuff and then hide the spoilers at the end. Don't read them unless you've read the book. I'm serious!!!!<br/><br/>First off, while Tim and Alice do have that fabulous odd couple chemistry going on (he's the recovering train wreck, she's the ti</span>
  <span id="freeText16079556738715604385" style="display:none">So ... whoa! This book was not at all what I expected. I did like <b>Boy Most Likely To</b>, but it took me some time to shift my mental gears around and adjust to the loss of the story I thought I was getting and warm up to the one I got. I'll talk about the non-spoilery stuff and then hide the spoilers at the end. Don't read them unless you've read the book. I'm serious!!!!<br /><br />First off, while Tim and Alice do have that fabulous odd couple chemistry going on (he's the recovering train wreck, she's the tightly-wound control freak) the Tim-Alice romance is really not the main focus of this book. Their relationship is so slow burn that ... is there a word for a notch below slow burn? Quiet simmer? That's what this felt like.<br /><br />To be fair, both Tim and Alice are very distracted with ... stuff that I'll discuss later under spoiler protection. Their relationship is pretty much at a standstill for about two-thirds of the book. Things eventually do heat up between them but it does take a while. In theory, I think it's a good thing that Tim is getting himself together before getting together with Alice, but if you're expecting a super-swoony book, you won't get that until the very end.<br /><br />The dual POV was a bit jarring to me -- a lot of switching back and forth, sometimes a few times within the same chapter. I was saved by the fact that each POV had a different font. I think MLND was all from Sam's POV and I think I might have preferred this from Tim's POV only.<br /><br />Now to the elephant in the room: that New Thing That Tim Has to Deal With. Yes, it did help Tim's character growth, but overall I was really on the fence about this aspect of the story. I thought some of those scenes in that plotline were funny and touching, but the whole thing took the story in an unexpected direction. I also must add that it kept reminding me of a very similar plot <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[ on Gossip Girl (the TV version.) Remember Dan and Georgina and baby Milo? Around season 3 or 4? Georgina shows up with baby Milo and Dan believes her when she says Milo is his child. Then Georgina vanishes and Dan has to take care of Milo, which helps him come to terms with the whole fatherhood thing and then ... Dan finds out he's being played. I did like the idea of Alice's plotline -- her control issues and her attempt to break free of her family and her standing up to Sam's mom. But to me it felt a bit like Alice's character growth had to take a back seat to the Baby Daddy Drama. <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br /><br />For the most part, I enjoyed this book. The storyline definitely wasn't what I expected but I'm always glad when a book can surprise me. I may re-read the two back to back now that I know what's to come.</span>
  <a data-text-id="16079556738715604385" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

The Boy Most Likely to is about Tin-Alice and Recovering Alcoholic Tim, who fall hard for each other against all odds, falling despite o</span>
  <span id="freeText534950808448967940" style="display:none"><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1433801983ra/15144777.gif" width="500" height="281" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Yep. That's exactly the way I'd react if Tim would be sitting opposite to me. If I were Brad and gay I'd prolly call him Timmyoyo. Timko. Timasaurous. Timato. Timbo. Blah blah. Annoying, eh?<br>This is Brad-mode, but I'll get to him later, 'cause first and foremost I'd like to thank Huntley Fitzpatrick for writeting this awesome book. Whoops, sorry, I mean writing. The Boy Most Likely to is about Tin-Alice and Recovering Alcoholic Tim, who fall hard for each other against all odds, falling despite of the train of siblings and responsibilities trailing behind Alice, despite Tim's past lurking right in front of him. The story isn't an ordinary one and that is what makes it special, the writing is extraordinary, the humour is real cool and the characters are filled with bruised-but-not-broken awesomeness! <br><br>When I read about Jase and Sam, I thought there couldn't be a sweeter teen couple, but man, I was wrong. I like Alice &amp; Tim a lot more. I mean Alcoholic and <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[teenage dad <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span> Tim still managed to be Hot in a very unique way. Alice, <i>Oh, Alice</i>, I just love her! Then there's Hester, who takes annoying to a whole new universe! <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[ I mean, man, she couldn't abort Cal but she sure as hell was looking forward to throwing him in the arms of any potential adoptive parents! And Cal? He was such a cutie! <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br><br>But, alas, there were somethings that I disliked about this book. <br>(a) The story is predictable. <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[ Knew from the beginning Cal wasn't Tim's and also that Jake and Nate would end up adopting him, how convenient, right? <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br>(b) <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[ Why didn't Tim get that blood test done at the first place? Silly even in a parallel universe.  <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br>(c) <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[ This 17 year old dude was a little too responsible, I mean not even a 27 year old man is, but that's okay.  <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br>(d) The book is dragged.<br><br>Well, no biggie, still love the book. This one is worth a read.<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1442838081ra/16283762.gif" width="400" height="352" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1573267434" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7404342331809158627">(Source: I received a digital copy of this book for free on a read-to-review basis. Thanks to Egmont Publishing and NetGalley.)<br/><br/><blockquote>

    <i>“Just like you didn’t let on that I was more full of drugs than a Pfizer warehouse.”</i>

</blockquote><br/><br/>This was a YA contemporary story, with a little bit of romance.<br/><br/>I didn’t really care for the characters in this book, Alice was okay, Tim was a bit of a screw-up, but I didn’t feel anything else for them really.<br/><br/>The storyline in this was a bit of a let-down for me, we got a stor</span>
  <span id="freeText7404342331809158627" style="display:none">(Source: I received a digital copy of this book for free on a read-to-review basis. Thanks to Egmont Publishing and NetGalley.)<br><br><blockquote>
  <b>
    <i>“Just like you didn’t let on that I was more full of drugs than a Pfizer warehouse.”</i>
  </b>
</blockquote><br><br>This was a YA contemporary story, with a little bit of romance.<br><br>I didn’t really care for the characters in this book, Alice was okay, Tim was a bit of a screw-up, but I didn’t feel anything else for them really.<br><br>The storyline in this was a bit of a let-down for me, we got a storyline about Tim facing an unexpected surprise, and Alice was having some money problems with her family, but there was very little happening on the romance front, and that was just disappointing for me.<br><br>The ending was again just okay, and I finished this book just feeling generally disappointed with it.<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1433066531i/15045433.png" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>6 out of 10</span>

<span id="freeTextContainer8716474728718558793">This book was just pretty meh to me. There were things I really liked and things I didn’t and it all kind of melded together into a just-okay book. I remember liking the boy next door a lot better, but it’s been a while since I read that! I was just on a contemporary kick and this was there so I went for it buuuuuuut I was kinda disappointed.<br/>I do like the narrative of Tim stepping up to the plate when he’s told he is a father - he is a super dynamic character and I loved seeing him grow. Alice, </span>
  <span id="freeText8716474728718558793" style="display:none">This book was just pretty meh to me. There were things I really liked and things I didn’t and it all kind of melded together into a just-okay book. I remember liking the boy next door a lot better, but it’s been a while since I read that! I was just on a contemporary kick and this was there so I went for it buuuuuuut I was kinda disappointed.<br />I do like the narrative of Tim stepping up to the plate when he’s told he is a father - he is a super dynamic character and I loved seeing him grow. Alice, however, fell a little flat for me. It felt like her story wasn’t as developed and I didn’t really know her as much as a character. <br />Overall an okay read but nothing amazing.</span>

<div id="review_757135105" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/757135105" />
    <a title="Alyssa" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/8472395-alyssa"><img alt="Alyssa" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1500935920p2/8472395.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/757135105?book_show_action=true">Nov 04, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Alyssa" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Alyssa" href="/user/show/8472395-alyssa">Alyssa</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9780803741423" href="/book/show/24611582-the-boy-most-likely-to">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/8472395-alyssa?shelf=2015-releases">2015-releases</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer757135105" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12699989722236410570">This book has been on my Goodreads shelf for nearly two years! :O<br/><br/><strong>My blog is the blog most likely to</strong>... <a href='http://eaterofbooks.blogspot.com/2015/06/the-blog-most-likely-to-and-giveaway.html' rel='nofollow noopener'>come find out</a>! And win a copy of <i>The Boy Most Likely To</i> while you're there! :D<br/><br/><strong>Another giveaway!</strong> <a href='http://eaterofbooks.blogspot.com/2015/07/review-and-giveaway-what-i-thought-was.html' rel='nofollow noopener'>Come see what I thought of <i>What I Thought Was True</i>, and enter to win <i>The Boy Most Likely To</i></a>!<br/><br/><strong>Be sure to explore </strong><a href='bit.ly/HuntleyFitzpatrickSampler' rel='nofollow noopener'>the first four chapters</a> of <i>The Boy Most Likely To</i> and help #UnlockTheBoy!<br/><br/><br/>***<a href='http://eaterofbooks.blogspot.com/2015/07/review-and-giveaway-boy-most-likely-to.html' rel='nofollow noopener'>Review posted on The Eater of Books! blog</a>***<br/><br/>The Boy Most Likely To by Huntley Fitzpatrick<br/>Book Two of the My Life N</span>
  <span id="freeText12699989722236410570" style="display:none">This book has been on my Goodreads shelf for nearly two years! :O<br /><br /><strong>My blog is the blog most likely to</strong>... <a href="http://eaterofbooks.blogspot.com/2015/06/the-blog-most-likely-to-and-giveaway.html" rel="nofollow noopener">come find out</a>! And win a copy of <i>The Boy Most Likely To</i> while you're there! :D<br /><br /><strong>Another giveaway!</strong> <a href="http://eaterofbooks.blogspot.com/2015/07/review-and-giveaway-what-i-thought-was.html" rel="nofollow noopener">Come see what I thought of <i>What I Thought Was True</i>, and enter to win <i>The Boy Most Likely To</i></a>!<br /><br /><strong>Be sure to explore </strong><a href="bit.ly/HuntleyFitzpatrickSampler" rel="nofollow noopener">the first four chapters</a> of <i>The Boy Most Likely To</i> and help #UnlockTheBoy!<br /><br /><br />***<a href="http://eaterofbooks.blogspot.com/2015/07/review-and-giveaway-boy-most-likely-to.html" rel="nofollow noopener">Review posted on The Eater of Books! blog</a>***<br /><br />The Boy Most Likely To by Huntley Fitzpatrick<br />Book Two of the My Life Next Door series<br />Publisher: Dial Books<br />Publication Date: August 18, 2015<br />Rating: 3 stars<br />Source: eARC from NetGalley<br /><br />Summary (from Goodreads):<br /><br />Tim Mason was The Boy Most Likely To find the liquor cabinet blindfolded, need a liver transplant, and drive his car into a house<br /><br />Alice Garrett was The Girl Most Likely To . . . well, not date her little brother’s baggage-burdened best friend, for starters.<br /><br />For Tim, it wouldn’t be smart to fall for Alice. For Alice, nothing could be scarier than falling for Tim. But Tim has never been known for making the smart choice, and Alice is starting to wonder if the “smart” choice is always the right one. When these two crash into each other, they crash hard.<br /><br />Then the unexpected consequences of Tim’s wild days come back to shock him. He finds himself in a situation that isn’t all it appears to be, that he never could have predicted . . . but maybe should have.<br /><br />And Alice is caught in the middle.<br /><br />Told in Tim’s and Alice’s distinctive, disarming, entirely compelling voices, this novel is for readers of The Spectacular Now, Nick and Norah’s Infinite Playlist, and Paper Towns. <br /><br />What I Liked:<br /><br />Ahhh, the bittersweet kiss of disappointment. I really wanted to like this one more than I did. I read My Life Next Door years ago, and LOVED it. I'm not a cotemporary fan, but this book was one of my favorite books ever - contemporary or otherwise. I just read What I Thought Was True last week, despite owning the book for a while. While I didn't love it as much as I loved My Life Next Door, I thought it was great! Huntley's first two novels were awesome. Five stars to the first one, four stars to the second one... three stars to the third one (The Boy Most Likely To). I can't believe I waited this long, only to be disappointed!<br /><br />Tim has been kicked out of high school, kicked out of his parents' house, and kicked out of his AA buddy's place, which he hadn't even started to live in yet. Tim's best friend Jase Garrett has Tim live in the Garrett's garage apartment. Alice, Jase's older sister, has been wanting to move into that garage apartment for a long time. With eight kids, the Garretts are quite a large family. Alice is nineteen, the second oldest, should be in college. Instead, she's taking of five of her younger siblings (with Jase, who is a year younger than Alice), while their mom is pregnant with Garrett #9 and their dad is in the hospital after a car accident. The last thing Alice needs is Tim taking the garage apartment. The last thing Tim needs is an unexpected surprise from someone he barely knows. Tim and Alice have way too much going on to be dabbling in a relationship - but maybe that is exactly what they need.<br /><br />I'm not sure if I was a fan of Tim in My Life Next Door, but remember thinking that he was a crazy kid who needed to get his life together. This book takes that statement to a whole different level. Tim's life is insane. His school kicked him out, his dad kicked him out, and now there is someone new in his life. Not to mention he's kicked alcohol, cigarettes, and drugs OUT of his life. Tim has got it all going on, but I like him. He turns everything into a joke, but he's actually pretty serious, straight-thinking, and smart.<br /><br />Alice is a control freak. She is always trying to keep Harry, George, Duff, Patsy, and Andy in line. Joel, the oldest Garrett kid, is on his own, living his life. Alice is the second, Jase is the third. Jase is going to college, but Alice had to defer, with the new Garrett baby and their father's injuries. Alice is a second mother, and a control freak. She likes being the dominate one in relationships, and is a bit of a heartless b****. Except around Tim.<br /><br />The romance is not like that of My Life Next Door or What I Thought Was True at all. While I personally found this to be disappointing, someone else might be pleased. There is little physical interactions between Alice and Tim for about 60% of the book.<br /><br />The conflict of the book pops in pretty quickly, and it seems a bit... I don't know, weird? I realize this could be an Alyssa thing, but I wasn't sure how I felt about the big curveball of the rising action. A friend of mine said it seemed "convenient", and I agree. It seemed like an easy way to draw this plot, an obvious way. But still, it was definitely fascinating. This plot dominates the story.<br /><br />One thing that I absolutely LOVED - this book is connected to What I Thought Was True! Which is a standalone that is completely unrelated to this series! Or so we thought. There is one character that links What I Thought Was True and this book - love love love! I may or may not have squealed when I read that character's name - even if I wasn't the biggest fan of the guy in What I Thought Was True ( still am not a fan).<br /><br />Overall, I liked the book - I just did not love it, and felt disappointed by it. After waiting so long, perhaps my expectations were too high. Or something.<br /><br />What I Did Not Like:<br /><br />Like I said above, I didn't really enjoy the big curveball of the rising action. There is a statement that Tim makes that foreshadows this Big Thing, but it seems weird to me. I had mixed feelings as I was reading, and I didn't seem to enjoy the story after The Big Thing was revealed (which is about 30% or so into the book? I'm bad at estimating. It seemed fairly early). The story kind of went downhill from there, for me. This isn't a fluffy contemporary romance novel - one could have figured that out, with Tim being an actively recovering alcoholic and substance abuser. But there is something else going on, and it's... weird. <br /><br />And the fact that Tim didn't do this one thing to begin with, after finding out about The Big Thing? Hint: he should have questioned the accuracy of what he was told from the start. It doesn't make you a d**khead - it makes you smart. Duh. <br /><br />The romance - this is not like Jase and Sam. This book is driven by something that is not related to Alice at all. The romance felt nonexistent, in my opinion. Either Huntley didn't do the best job of fleshing out the romance, or she did, and it's supposed to be a bit not-there and subtle and whatnot. Insta-love-y, in my opinion. Did Tim already like Alice from My Life Next Door? I can't remember. But their romance started off insta-love-y, and then there were a ton of speed-bumps and obstacles, and then finally at the end, there is a resolution. The romance was not enjoyable. <br /><br />Also, there was something that Huntley did not tie up well. I personally think she left the audience hanging when it came to Brad. I won't explain who Brad is, or his role in the book, but just know that Huntley did not resolve his part of the book. I thought he would play a huge role in some part of the climax, but nope!<br /><br />This is going to make me seem judgmental - but I've seen many people say that they would LOVE to be a Garrett, for the Garrett's to adopt them. Personally, I would hate that. Eight kids, ninth on the way, no money, not even to feed the children? I personally would not even bring ONE child into the world if I couldn't somehow provide. But nine?! And your oldest is twenty-two?! My paternal grandmother did this, guys. Ten children - nine boys, one girl. My dad is the youngest. He and several of the other younger children were raised by the oldest children. It was in a third-world country with things like dirt floors and no running water or electricity. The Garretts are in the USA with all of these great things that they can't pay for and are STILL making more children. I don't know, seems like a bad idea to me. Especially since we get to see things from the second oldest's POV - Alice - and remember, Joel is the twenty-two, the oldest and no longer lives at home. It's so unfair to Alice that she has to take care of her siblings! She does it out of love and blah blah blah but it's still very, very unfair. <br /><br />Anyway. To each their own. Big families are fun, according to my dad (and my mom, who had seven siblings). But I have two older siblings and they are two enough. Not for me! Again, I realize this is a personal thing. But coming from large families? Taught me a few things.<br /><br />This might be an Advanced Reader Copy thing, but distinguishing between Alice and Tim's POV was so annoying! There were no asterisks or names in bold at the beginning of a new POV, nothing to indicate a switch. Maybe this will be fixed in the final copy.<br /><br />Anyway... there were some other things I didn't really like about this book, but I'll step aside for now.<br /><br />Would I Recommend It:<br /><br />This is a hard book to recommend/not recommend. On the one hand, I really enjoy Huntley's contemporary books, and would technically recommend any of them. On the other hand, this is easily Huntley's weakest. And yet it took the longest to appear. Definitely read My Life Next Door, but you could stop there. I know there are many Huntley readers that are very devoted, like me, and will read this one no matter what and/or will buy it no matter what. More power to you! I would do the same, had I not read it early.<br /><br />Rating:<br /><br />3 stars. It's with a heavy heart that I give this book less than four stars. I mean, it could have been two-star or one-star bad though. Three stars isn't terrible. It isn't that great, either. I liked this book, but I expected so much better, and ended up being disappointed.</span>
  <a data-text-id="12699989722236410570" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_756179758" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/756179758" />
    <a title="nick (the infinite limits of love)" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2993271-nick-the-infinite-limits-of-love"><img alt="nick (the infinite limits of love)" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1606193187p2/2993271.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/756179758?book_show_action=true">Nov 03, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="nick (the infinite limits of love)" class="user" itemprop="url" name="nick (the infinite limits of love)" href="/user/show/2993271-nick-the-infinite-limits-of-love">nick (the infinite limits of love)</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9780803741423" href="/book/show/24611582-the-boy-most-likely-to">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2993271-nick-the-infinite-limits-of-love?shelf=arc">arc</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer756179758" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13628549592961559019"><br/>You know what's one of the <b>worst feelings ever</b>? Not loving a book that you've been waiting forever for from a favorite author. It's no secret that Huntley Fitzpatrick is an <b>auto-buy author </b>for me as she is for many other readers. Her debut book especially holds a <b>special place</b> on my book shelf. When I found out that she was going to revisit the Garretts and Tim from <i>My Life Next Door,</i> I was eager to get a copy of <i>The Boy Most Likely To</i>. I don't know if it was the <b>high expectations</b>, but <i>The Boy M</i></span>
  <span id="freeText13628549592961559019" style="display:none"><br />You know what's one of the <b>worst feelings ever</b>? Not loving a book that you've been waiting forever for from a favorite author. It's no secret that Huntley Fitzpatrick is an <b>auto-buy author </b>for me as she is for many other readers. Her debut book especially holds a <b>special place</b> on my book shelf. When I found out that she was going to revisit the Garretts and Tim from <i>My Life Next Door,</i> I was eager to get a copy of <i>The Boy Most Likely To</i>. I don't know if it was the <b>high expectations</b>, but <i>The Boy Most Likely To</i> <b>wasn't as memorable</b> for me as the author's previous books.<br /><br />While this book is told in the dual POVs of Tim and Alice, Tim got the most page space. From book 1, we know that Tim was a boy who had a rather <b>rough family life</b> and that he was <b>struggling</b> with a lot. Being inside Tim's head wasn't always the easiest, to be honest and while I think Huntley Fitzpatrick did a <b>lovely job at crafting the male POV </b>with an authentic voice, I wasn't able to completely connect with his character. I think my main issue with this book was that Tim had all these problems in his life - <b>alcoholism, shitty parents, strained sibling relationships, being kicked out of school</b> - but I wasn't sure where they all stemmed from. I needed to get a good grasp of where all his emerging from and while we may be told briefly, I wasn't convinced by it. And then when the <b>big twist</b> came up, I was a little bit <b>frustrated</b> because everything seemed so <b>excessive</b>. The boy was already battling with so much, so to have yet another storm smack him in the face seemed just a bit too much. That being said, this twist did push Tim to finally <b>grow up</b> slowly over the course of the book but by the end, I still felt like Tim had much growing to do. I will admit that Tim could be very <b>endearing</b> when he showed his more <b>lighthearted side</b>, especially when it came to Patsy and Alice Garrett, but I'm sad that I didn't love him as much as I loved Jase. I felt similarly towards Alice. She didn't have that spark and energy that I found in Sam in<i> My Life Next Door.</i> I don't particularly have much to say about her because she <b>wasn't memorable</b> for me. I did, however, <b>love seeing the Garretts </b>again, especially George who continued to be the cutest boy ever.<br /><br />The romance between Tim and Alice was very slow to develop, sometimes, <b>excruciatingly slow</b>. Part of me thought that the romance was a little bit <b>lacking</b> because I wanted to see more of Tim and Alice together. The moments we did have of them though were <b>very sweet</b> and I think if there had been more scenes I would have fallen for this couple just as much as I fell for Sam and Jase. Like I mentioned before, there was just so much going on in this book not only with Tim, but also with Alice having to deal with her dad's accident and her having to upend her entire life to take care of her siblings. It's clear that Huntley Fitzpatrick wanted to<b> tackle all these themes</b> in her book, but it made for <b>a mess</b>, in my opinion, <b>with none of the themes well-fleshed out</b>. This book had the <b>potential to turn me into a blubbering sobbing mess</b>, but because all of the issues were skimmed upon, they came across as weak and <b>did not have that strong of an emotional punch</b> as it could have had. I do think this could have been achieved if the focus had been on one or two themes and building up those themes to perfection. Even with the issues I had with <i>The Boy Most Likely</i>, I l<b>oved Huntley Fitzpatrick's writing</b>, which is why I pushed through 432 pages of this book. While this may not have been her strongest book for me personally, I will continue to pick up anything that she writes because her writing is so lovely.<br /><br />One of my recurring thoughts while I was reading <i>The Boy Most Likely To</i> was that it r<b>ead a lot like an angsty New Adult book</b>. So even though this was a bit of a <b>disappointment </b>for me, I appear to be a bit of a black sheep. I think if you are a reader that <b>enjoys angst in their books</b> together with <b>more mature storylines</b>, <i>The Boy Most Likely To</i> will work wonderfully for you.<br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="13628549592961559019" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>
